   <p id="mwCg">
    The
    <i id="mwCw">
     <a href="./James_Bond" id="mwDA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond">
      James Bond
     </a>
    </i>
    video game franchise is a series centering on
    <a href="./Ian_Fleming" id="mwDQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Ian Fleming">
     Ian Fleming
    </a>
    's fictional British
    <a href="./Secret_Intelligence_Service" id="mwDg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Secret Intelligence Service">
     MI6
    </a>
    agent,
    <a href="./James_Bond_(literary_character)" id="mwDw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond (literary character)">
     James Bond
    </a>
    . Games of the series have been predominantly
    <a href="./Shooter_game" id="mwEA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Shooter game">
     shooter games
    </a>
    , with some games of other genres including
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Role-playing_video_games" id="mwEQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Role-playing video games">
     role-playing
    </a>
    and
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Adventure_games" id="mwEg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Adventure games">
     adventure games
    </a>
    . Several games are based upon the
    <a href="./Production_of_the_James_Bond_films" id="mwEw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Production of the James Bond films">
     <i id="mwFA">
      James Bond
     </i>
     films
    </a>
    and developed and published by a variety of companies,  The intellectual property is owned by
    <a href="./Danjaq" id="mwFQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Danjaq">
     Danjaq
    </a>
    .
   </p>
  </section>

      </td>

   <section data-mw-section-id="2" id="mwGQ">
    <h3 id="Early_era_(1983–1994)">
     <span id="Early_era_.281983.E2.80.931994.29" typeof="mw:FallbackId">
     </span>
     Early era (1983–1994)
    </h3>
    <p id="mwGg">
     In 1983,
     <a href="./Parker_Brothers" id="mwGw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Parker Brothers">
      Parker Brothers
     </a>
     released the first officially licensed
     <a href="./James_Bond" id="mwHA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond">
      James Bond
     </a>
     video game,
     <a href="./James_Bond_007_(1983_video_game)" id="mwHQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007 (1983 video game)">
      <i id="mwHg">
       James Bond 007
      </i>
     </a>
     , for multiple platforms.
     <sup about="#mwt16" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-1"}}' id="cite_ref-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-1" id="mwHw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 1;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwIA">
        [1]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     An earlier unofficial game,
     <i id="mwIQ">
      <a href="./Shaken_but_Not_Stirred" id="mwIg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Shaken but Not Stirred">
       Shaken but Not Stirred
      </a>
     </i>
     , had been released in 1982.
     <sup about="#mwt20" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-2"}}' id="cite_ref-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-2" id="mwIw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 2;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwJA">
        [2]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwJQ">
     Since 1983, there have been numerous video games based on the films,
     <a href="./Ian_Fleming" id="mwJg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Ian Fleming">
      Ian Fleming
     </a>
     's novels, and original scripts created by the
     <a href="./Video_game_developer" id="mwJw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Video game developer">
      developer
     </a>
     or
     <a href="./Video_game_publisher" id="mwKA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Video game publisher">
      publisher
     </a>
     of the game.
     <a href="./Mindscape_(company)" id="mwKQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Mindscape (company)">
      Mindscape
     </a>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt28" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-3"}}' id="cite_ref-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-3" id="mwKg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 3;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwKw">
        [3]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Domark" id="mwLA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Domark">
      Domark
     </a>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt32" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-4"}}' id="cite_ref-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-4" id="mwLQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 4;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwLg">
        [4]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <a href="./Interplay_Entertainment" id="mwLw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Interplay Entertainment">
      Interplay
     </a>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt36" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-5"}}' id="cite_ref-5" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-5" id="mwMA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 5;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwMQ">
        [5]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     and
     <a href="./THQ" id="mwMg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="THQ">
      THQ
     </a>
     <sup about="#mwt40" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-6"}}' id="cite_ref-6" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-6" id="mwMw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 6;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwNA">
        [6]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     all created James Bond games.
    </p>
    <p id="mwNQ">
     The video games were somewhat profitable
     <link about="#mwt41" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"Citation needed","href":"./Template:Citation_needed"},"params":{"date":{"wt":"October 2020"}},"i":0}}]}' href="./Category:All_articles_with_unsourced_statements" id="mwNg" rel="mw:PageProp/Category" typeof="mw:Transclusion"/>
     <link about="#mwt41" href="./Category:Articles_with_unsourced_statements_from_October_2020" rel="mw:PageProp/Category"/>
     <sup about="#mwt41" class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" id="mwNw" style="white-space:nowrap;">
      <span typeof="mw:Entity">
       [
      </span>
      <i>
       <a href="./Wikipedia:Citation_needed" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
        <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">
         citation needed
        </span>
       </a>
      </i>
      <span typeof="mw:Entity">
       ]
      </span>
     </sup>
     in the 1980s and early 1990s, featuring a mixture of styles including
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Side-scroller" id="mwOA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Side-scroller">
      side-scrolling
     </a>
     action and
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Text_adventure" id="mwOQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Text adventure">
      text adventure
     </a>
     .
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="3" id="mwOg">
    <h3 id="Nintendo_era_(1995–1998)">
     <span id="Nintendo_era_.281995.E2.80.931998.29" typeof="mw:FallbackId">
     </span>
     Nintendo era (1995–1998)
    </h3>
    <p id="mwOw">
     The popularity of the James Bond video game series did not rise quickly until 1997's
     <i id="mwPA">
      <a href="./GoldenEye_007_(1997_video_game)" id="mwPQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye 007 (1997 video game)">
       GoldenEye 007
      </a>
     </i>
     by
     <a href="./Rare_(company)" id="mwPg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Rare (company)">
      Rare
     </a>
     for the
     <a href="./Nintendo_64" id="mwPw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Nintendo 64">
      Nintendo 64
     </a>
     .
     <i id="mwQA">
      GoldenEye 007
     </i>
     expanded on the plot of the film
     <i id="mwQQ">
      <a href="./GoldenEye" id="mwQg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye">
       GoldenEye
      </a>
     </i>
     and is a
     <a href="./First-person_shooter" id="mwQw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="First-person shooter">
      first-person shooter
     </a>
     with a
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Multiplayer" id="mwRA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Multiplayer">
      multiplayer
     </a>
     mode.
     <sup about="#mwt48" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-7"}}' id="cite_ref-7" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-7" id="mwRQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 7;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwRg">
        [7]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game received very positive reviews
     <sup about="#mwt52" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"gamerankings"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-gamerankings-8"}}' id="cite_ref-gamerankings_8-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-gamerankings-8" id="mwRw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 8;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwSA">
        [8]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     and sold over eight million copies.
     <sup about="#mwt56" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"8million"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-8million-9"}}' id="cite_ref-8million_9-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-8million-9" id="mwSQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 9;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwSg">
        [9]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwSw">
     In 1998,
     <a href="./Nintendo" id="mwTA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Nintendo">
      Nintendo
     </a>
     released
     <i id="mwTQ">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007_(1998_video_game)" id="mwTg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007 (1998 video game)">
       James Bond 007
      </a>
     </i>
     for the
     <a href="./Game_Boy" id="mwTw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Game Boy">
      Game Boy
     </a>
     developed by
     <a href="./Saffire_(company)" id="mwUA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Saffire (company)">
      Saffire
     </a>
     . The game features a story including characters from multiple James Bond films, such as
     <a href="./Oddjob" id="mwUQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Oddjob">
      Oddjob
     </a>
     and
     <a href="./Jaws_(James_Bond)" id="mwUg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Jaws (James Bond)">
      Jaws
     </a>
     . It also incorporates gambling
     <a href="./Minigame" id="mwUw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Minigame">
      minigames
     </a>
     , such as
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Baccarat_(card_game)" id="mwVA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Baccarat (card game)">
      Baccarat
     </a>
     and
     <a href="./Blackjack" id="mwVQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Blackjack">
      Blackjack
     </a>
     .
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="4" id="mwVg">
    <h3 id="Electronic_Arts_era_(1999–2005)">
     <span id="Electronic_Arts_era_.281999.E2.80.932005.29" typeof="mw:FallbackId">
     </span>
     Electronic Arts era (1999–2005)
    </h3>
    <p id="mwVw">
     <a href="./Electronic_Arts" id="mwWA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Electronic Arts">
      Electronic Arts
     </a>
     took over the license from MGM Interactive when a video game based on
     <i id="mwWQ">
      <a href="./Tomorrow_Never_Dies" id="mwWg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">
       Tomorrow Never Dies
      </a>
     </i>
     was in development in 1998. Taking the initial concepts for the
     <a href="./Tomorrow_Never_Dies_(video_game)" id="mwWw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Tomorrow Never Dies (video game)">
      video game adaptation
     </a>
     , developer
     <a href="./Black_Ops_Entertainment" id="mwXA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Black Ops Entertainment">
      Black Ops Entertainment
     </a>
     handled the final form of the title and the game saw the light of day in 1999 on
     <a href="./PlayStation_(console)" id="mwXQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="PlayStation (console)">
      PlayStation
     </a>
     <sup about="#mwt63" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-10"}}' id="cite_ref-10" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-10" id="mwXg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 10;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwXw">
        [10]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     and met mixed reviews from critics, albeit becoming a financial success. The following entry was to be based on
     <i id="mwYA">
      <a href="./The_World_Is_Not_Enough" id="mwYQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="The World Is Not Enough">
       The World Is Not Enough
      </a>
     </i>
     , consisting of several versions released on multiple platforms, including one on
     <a href="./The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(Nintendo_64)" id="mwYg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="The World Is Not Enough (Nintendo 64)">
      Nintendo 64
     </a>
     developed by
     <a href="./Eurocom" id="mwYw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eurocom">
      Eurocom
     </a>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt67" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-11"}}' id="cite_ref-11" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-11" id="mwZA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 11;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwZQ">
        [11]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     a version for
     <a href="./The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(PlayStation)" id="mwZg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="The World Is Not Enough (PlayStation)">
      PlayStation
     </a>
     developed by Black Ops Entertainment, and
     <a href="./The_World_Is_Not_Enough_(2001_video_game)" id="mwZw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="The World Is Not Enough (2001 video game)">
      Game Boy Color
     </a>
     by 2n Productions, with all three meeting different results in spite of being commercially successful. Unlike the former two versions – first-person shooters – the Game Boy Color version is played from a top-down perspective.
     <sup about="#mwt71" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"ALL"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-ALL-12"}}' id="cite_ref-ALL_12-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-ALL-12" id="mwaA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwaQ">
        [12]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwag">
     In 2001, EA released
     <i id="mwaw">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Agent_Under_Fire" id="mwbA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Agent Under Fire">
       Agent Under Fire
      </a>
     </i>
     for
     <a href="./PlayStation_2" id="mwbQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="PlayStation 2">
      PlayStation 2
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="./GameCube" id="mwbg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GameCube">
      GameCube
     </a>
     , and
     <a href="./Xbox_(console)" id="mwbw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Xbox (console)">
      Xbox
     </a>
     , featuring an original storyline
     <sup about="#mwt77" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-13"}}' id="cite_ref-13" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-13" id="mwcA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 13;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwcQ">
        [13]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     and lacking the likeness of then Bond actor
     <a href="./Pierce_Brosnan" id="mwcg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Pierce Brosnan">
      Pierce Brosnan
     </a>
     .
     <sup about="#mwt81" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-14"}}' id="cite_ref-14" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-14" id="mwcw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 14;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwdA">
        [14]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game added the elements of "rail" shooting and driving segments to a first-person shooter. The game sold nearly 5 million copies, making it the second-most successful game in the series, while only receiving mixed reviews. There are no differences between the console versions.
    </p>
    <p id="mwdQ">
     In 2002,
     <i id="mwdg">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Nightfire" id="mwdw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Nightfire">
       Nightfire
      </a>
     </i>
     was released, coinciding with the 40th anniversary of the film franchise and using Brosnan's likeness for the Bond character, but not his voice.
     <sup about="#mwt86" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-15"}}' id="cite_ref-15" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-15" id="mweA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 15;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mweQ">
        [15]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     It was developed by
     <a href="./Eurocom" id="mweg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eurocom">
      Eurocom
     </a>
     for the GameCube, PlayStation 2, and Xbox consoles, with a
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Personal_computer_game" id="mwew" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Personal computer game">
      PC
     </a>
     port by
     <a href="./Gearbox_Software" id="mwfA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Gearbox Software">
      Gearbox Software
     </a>
     and a
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Mac_OS_X" id="mwfQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Mac OS X">
      Mac
     </a>
     port by
     <a href="./Aspyr" id="mwfg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Aspyr">
      Aspyr
     </a>
     . The computer versions are substantially different from the console versions, featuring different missions, a modified story line, and online play. In 2003, the game also had a
     <a href="./Game_Boy_Advance" id="mwfw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Game Boy Advance">
      Game Boy Advance
     </a>
     version by
     <a href="./JV_Games" id="mwgA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="JV Games">
      JV Games
     </a>
     , which also differs from both the console versions and PC versions.
    </p>
    <p id="mwgQ">
     In 2004, EA released
     <i id="mwgg">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Everything_or_Nothing" id="mwgw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Everything or Nothing">
       Everything or Nothing
      </a>
     </i>
     , developed by EA Redwood, for the GameCube, PlayStation 2 and Xbox. Unlike the two previous installments,
     <i id="mwhA">
      Everything or Nothing
     </i>
     is a
     <a href="./Third-person_shooter" id="mwhQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Third-person shooter">
      third-person shooter
     </a>
     with driving missions, and it stars the voices and likenesses of
     <a href="./Pierce_Brosnan" id="mwhg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Pierce Brosnan">
      Pierce Brosnan
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="./Judi_Dench" id="mwhw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Judi Dench">
      Judi Dench
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="./Willem_Dafoe" id="mwiA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Willem Dafoe">
      Willem Dafoe
     </a>
     and
     <a href="./John_Cleese" id="mwiQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="John Cleese">
      John Cleese
     </a>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt91" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-16"}}' id="cite_ref-16" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-16" id="mwig" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 16;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwiw">
        [16]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     among others. It was written by the scriptwriter of
     <i id="mwjA">
      GoldenEye
     </i>
     and
     <i id="mwjQ">
      Tomorrow Never Dies
     </i>
     , screenwriter
     <a href="./Bruce_Feirstein" id="mwjg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Bruce Feirstein">
      Bruce Feirstein
     </a>
     , with a plot connected to the
     <a href="./Roger_Moore" id="mwjw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Roger Moore">
      Roger Moore
     </a>
     Bond film
     <i id="mwkA">
      <a href="./A_View_to_a_Kill" id="mwkQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="A View to a Kill">
       A View to a Kill
      </a>
     </i>
     . It was released to mostly positive reviews. A different version of
     <i id="mwkg">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Everything_or_Nothing_(GBA_video_game)" id="mwkw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Everything or Nothing (GBA video game)">
       Everything or Nothing
      </a>
     </i>
     was also developed by
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Griptonite_Games" id="mwlA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Griptonite Games">
      Griptonite Games
     </a>
     for the
     <a href="./Game_Boy_Advance" id="mwlQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Game Boy Advance">
      Game Boy Advance
     </a>
     .
    </p>
    <p id="mwlg">
     Later that year,
     <i id="mwlw">
      <a href="./GoldenEye:_Rogue_Agent" id="mwmA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye: Rogue Agent">
       GoldenEye: Rogue Agent
      </a>
     </i>
     was released on the same platforms with the exception of the Game Boy Advance version. A first-person shooter loosely connected to the Bond franchise a spin-off, it stars a former MI6 spy
     <sup about="#mwt96" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-17"}}' id="cite_ref-17" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-17" id="mwmQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 17;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwmg">
        [17]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     known as "GoldenEye", who works for
     <a href="./Auric_Goldfinger" id="mwmw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Auric Goldfinger">
      Auric Goldfinger
     </a>
     against
     <a href="./Julius_No" id="mwnA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Julius No">
      Dr. Julius No
     </a>
     . The game was panned for its misleading title and poor storyline. The game was released on PlayStation 2, Xbox, GameCube and Nintendo DS. EA listed
     <i id="mwnQ">
      007 Racing
     </i>
     and
     <i id="mwng">
      GoldenEye: Rogue Agent
     </i>
     as spin-offs, out of their canonical order they have built.
    </p>
    <p id="mwnw">
     2005 saw the release of
     <i id="mwoA">
      <a href="./From_Russia_with_Love_(video_game)" id="mwoQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="From Russia with Love (video game)">
       From Russia with Love
      </a>
     </i>
     , based on the 1963
     <a href="./From_Russia_with_Love_(film)" id="mwog" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="From Russia with Love (film)">
      film of the same name
     </a>
     . It stars
     <a href="./Sean_Connery" id="mwow" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Sean Connery">
      Sean Connery
     </a>
     as James Bond, and the other characters had the same likeness of the original cast. The game is a third-person shooter in the same style as
     <i id="mwpA">
      Everything or Nothing
     </i>
     , with expansions in the story and certain details changed (such as trading
     <a href="./SPECTRE" id="mwpQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="SPECTRE">
      SPECTRE
     </a>
     for OCTOPUS, due to
     <a href="./Thunderball_(novel)#Controversy" id="mwpg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Thunderball (novel)">
      legal problems
     </a>
     ).
     <sup about="#mwt101" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-18"}}' id="cite_ref-18" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-18" id="mwpw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 18;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwqA">
        [18]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game received positive reviews, and was released on GameCube, Xbox, PS2 and PSP.
    </p>
    <p id="mwqQ">
     Electronic Arts announced in 2006 a game based on then-upcoming
     <i id="mwqg">
      <a href="./Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" id="mwqw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">
       Casino Royale
      </a>
     </i>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt108" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"EA CR"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-EA_CR-19"}}' id="cite_ref-EA_CR_19-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-EA_CR-19" id="mwrA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwrQ">
        [19]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <sup about="#mwt112" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"LostGame"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-LostGame-20"}}' id="cite_ref-LostGame_20-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-LostGame-20" id="mwrg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 20;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwrw">
        [20]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     but it ended up being cancelled, because it would not be ready by the film's release in November. This fact, which would lead
     <a href="./Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" id="mwsA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">
      MGM
     </a>
     to lose millions in licensing fees, along with EA's commitment to move away from movie franchise games and focus more on internal intellectual properties, led the company to abandon the Bond franchise in May 2006.
     <sup about="#mwt116" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Fritz"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Fritz-21"}}' id="cite_ref-Fritz_21-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-Fritz-21" id="mwsQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 21;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwsg">
        [21]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="5" id="mwsw">
    <h3 id="Activision_era_(2006–2013)">
     <span id="Activision_era_.282006.E2.80.932013.29" typeof="mw:FallbackId">
     </span>
     Activision era (2006–2013)
    </h3>
    <p id="mwtA">
     Shortly after Electronic Arts abandoned the license, in May 2006,
     <a href="./Activision" id="mwtQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Activision">
      Activision
     </a>
     acquired non-exclusive rights to develop and publish James Bond games, which were to become exclusive in 2007.
     <sup about="#mwt123" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-22"}}' id="cite_ref-22" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-22" id="mwtg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 22;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwtw">
        [22]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     Activision's first game was
     <i id="mwuA">
      <a href="./007:_Quantum_of_Solace" id="mwuQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007: Quantum of Solace">
       Quantum of Solace
      </a>
     </i>
     , which was based on the 2008
     <a href="./Quantum_of_Solace" id="mwug" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Quantum of Solace">
      film of the same name
     </a>
     as well as the previous film
     <i id="mwuw">
      Casino Royale
     </i>
     .
     <sup about="#mwt127" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-23"}}' id="cite_ref-23" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-23" id="mwvA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 23;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwvQ">
        [23]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     It was developed by
     <a href="./Treyarch" id="mwvg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Treyarch">
      Treyarch
     </a>
     for PlayStation 3, Xbox 360, Wii and PC;
     <a href="./Eurocom" id="mwvw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eurocom">
      Eurocom
     </a>
     for PlayStation 2 and
     <a href="./Vicarious_Visions" id="mwwA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Vicarious Visions">
      Vicarious Visions
     </a>
     for the Nintendo DS. The game was released on 31 October 2008 and received mixed reviews, with the PlayStation 2 version receiving the best reviews.
     <sup about="#mwt131" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-24"}}' id="cite_ref-24" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-24" id="mwwQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 24;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwwg">
        [24]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwww">
     At
     <a href="./E3_2010" id="mwxA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="E3 2010">
      E3 2010
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="./Nintendo" id="mwxQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Nintendo">
      Nintendo
     </a>
     revealed
     <i id="mwxg">
      <a href="./GoldenEye_007_(2010_video_game)" id="mwxw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye 007 (2010 video game)">
       GoldenEye 007
      </a>
     </i>
     , a remake for the
     <a href="./Wii" id="mwyA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Wii">
      Wii
     </a>
     of the 1997 game. Developed by
     <a href="./Eurocom" id="mwyQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eurocom">
      Eurocom
     </a>
     , using their
     <i id="mwyg">
      <a href="./Dead_Space:_Extraction" id="mwyw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Dead Space: Extraction">
       Dead Space: Extraction
      </a>
     </i>
     <a href="./Game_engine" id="mwzA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Game engine">
      game engine
     </a>
     , the game updated the story of the movie, with a script by
     <a href="./Bruce_Feirstein" id="mwzQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Bruce Feirstein">
      Bruce Feirstein
     </a>
     and the current Bond actor
     <a href="./Daniel_Craig" id="mwzg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Daniel Craig">
      Daniel Craig
     </a>
     as 007.
     <sup about="#mwt136" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-25"}}' id="cite_ref-25" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-25" id="mwzw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 25;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw0A">
        [25]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     It was released in November 2010 in all regions and received positive reviews from critics. Approximately a year later, an enhanced port of the game entitled
     <i id="mw0Q">
      GoldenEye 007: Reloaded
     </i>
     was released for PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360. The port featured HD graphics, new missions and
     <a href="./PlayStation_Move" id="mw0g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="PlayStation Move">
      PlayStation Move
     </a>
     support on the PS3 version.
    </p>
    <p id="mw0w">
     Activision's third Bond game,
     <i id="mw1A">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Blood_Stone" id="mw1Q" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Blood Stone">
       Blood Stone
      </a>
     </i>
     was released on the same day as
     <i id="mw1g">
      GoldenEye 007
     </i>
     in November 2010. Developed by
     <a href="./Bizarre_Creations" id="mw1w" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Bizarre Creations">
      Bizarre Creations
     </a>
     , the game returned to being a third person shooter, featured an original story and starred Daniel Craig, Judi Dench
     <sup about="#mwt142" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-26"}}' id="cite_ref-26" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-26" id="mw2A" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 26;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw2Q">
        [26]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     and
     <a href="./Joss_Stone" id="mw2g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Joss Stone">
      Joss Stone
     </a>
     , the latter of which also sang on the game's theme song "I'll Take it All".
     <sup about="#mwt146" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-27"}}' id="cite_ref-27" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-27" id="mw2w" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 27;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw3A">
        [27]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     It was released for PlayStation 3, Xbox 360, PC and DS and received mixed reviews from critics. Developer Bizarre Creations was closed down by Activision in early 2011 just a few months after the game's release.
    </p>
    <p id="mw3Q">
     On 19 April 2012,
     <a href="./Activision" id="mw3g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Activision">
      Activision
     </a>
     announced plans for a game titled
     <i id="mw3w">
      <a href="./007_Legends" id="mw4A" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007 Legends">
       007 Legends
      </a>
     </i>
     to coincide with the fiftieth anniversary of
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./James_Bond_in_film" id="mw4Q" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond in film">
      the James Bond film franchise
     </a>
     .
     <sup about="#mwt154" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Empire"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Empire-28"}}' id="cite_ref-Empire_28-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-Empire-28" id="mw4g" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 28;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw4w">
        [28]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game was described as a "greatest hits compilation",
     <sup about="#mwt155" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Empire"}}' id="cite_ref-Empire_28-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-Empire-28" id="mw5A" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 28;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw5Q">
        [28]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     retelling six film narratives with an overarching storyline to connect them together. The missions were revealed to be based upon
     <i id="mw5g">
      <a href="./Goldfinger_(film)" id="mw5w" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Goldfinger (film)">
       Goldfinger
      </a>
     </i>
     ,
     <i id="mw6A">
      <a href="./On_Her_Majesty's_Secret_Service_(film)" id="mw6Q" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="On Her Majesty's Secret Service (film)">
       On Her Majesty's Secret Service
      </a>
     </i>
     ,
     <i id="mw6g">
      <a href="./Moonraker_(film)" id="mw6w" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Moonraker (film)">
       Moonraker
      </a>
     </i>
     ,
     <i id="mw7A">
      <a href="./Licence_to_Kill" id="mw7Q" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Licence to Kill">
       Licence to Kill
      </a>
     </i>
     and
     <i id="mw7g">
      <a href="./Die_Another_Day" id="mw7w" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Die Another Day">
       Die Another Day
      </a>
     </i>
     . On 9 November 2012, Activision added the last mission to the game, released as a downloadable content, which was based on
     <i id="mw8A">
      <a href="./Skyfall" id="mw8Q" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Skyfall">
       Skyfall
      </a>
     </i>
     . The game was released for PlayStation 3, Xbox 360, PC and
     <a href="./Wii_U" id="mw8g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Wii U">
      Wii U
     </a>
     and received mixed reviews from critics. Developer
     <a href="./Eurocom" id="mw8w" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eurocom">
      Eurocom
     </a>
     shut down soon after the game's release in December 2012.
     <sup about="#mwt160" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-29"}}' id="cite_ref-29" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-29" id="mw9A" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 29;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw9Q">
        [29]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <sup about="#mwt164" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-30"}}' id="cite_ref-30" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-30" id="mw9g" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 30;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw9w">
        [30]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mw-A">
     On 4 January 2013, Activision and Steam's online stores removed online availability and pages for
     <i id="mw-Q">
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Quantum_of_Solace_(video_game)" id="mw-g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Quantum of Solace (video game)">
       Quantum of Solace
      </a>
     </i>
     ,
     <i id="mw-w">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Blood_Stone" id="mw_A" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Blood Stone">
       Blood Stone
      </a>
     </i>
     , and
     <i id="mw_Q">
      <a href="./007_Legends" id="mw_g" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007 Legends">
       007 Legends
      </a>
     </i>
     without explanation or warning,
     <sup about="#mwt171" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-31"}}' id="cite_ref-31" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-31" id="mw_w" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 31;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQA">
        [31]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     only to confirm three days later that the James Bond game license was revoked.
     <sup about="#mwt175" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-32"}}' id="cite_ref-32" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-32" id="mwAQE" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 32;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQI">
        [32]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     A month later, Activision themselves declared that they would be backing away from licensed games in a formal statement.
     <sup about="#mwt179" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-33"}}' id="cite_ref-33" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-33" id="mwAQM" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 33;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQQ">
        [33]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="6" id="mwAQU">
    <h3 id="Hiatus_and_IO_Interactive_era_(2020–present)">
     <span id="Hiatus_and_IO_Interactive_era_.282020.E2.80.93present.29" typeof="mw:FallbackId">
     </span>
     Hiatus and IO Interactive era (2020–present)
    </h3>
    <p id="mwAQY">
     On 7 January 2014, president and co-founder of
     <a href="./Telltale_Games" id="mwAQc" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Telltale Games">
      Telltale Games
     </a>
     , Kevin Bruner had expressed an interest in making a future James Bond game if he were afforded the chance. He stated that "I'm a giant James Bond fan and I'm always frustrated by games that make him a mass murderer." When he was asked which license he would adapt next if money and licensing hurdles were not a factor. "He's a super-spy, and that's a different skillset. The films make him less of a mass murderer, and there's not much killing in the books – more spying and intrigue."
     <sup about="#mwt186" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-34"}}' id="cite_ref-34" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-34" id="mwAQg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 34;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQk">
        [34]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     A rumour surfaced in June 2017 that Telltale was working on a video game entitled
     <i id="mwAQo">
      007 Solstice
     </i>
     .
     <sup about="#mwt190" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-35"}}' id="cite_ref-35" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-35" id="mwAQs" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 35;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQw">
        [35]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     However, its status proved unlikely when Telltale filed for bankruptcy and closed down in November 2018.
     <sup about="#mwt194" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-36"}}' id="cite_ref-36" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-36" id="mwAQ0" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 36;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQ4">
        [36]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwAQ8">
     On 21 January 2016, president of
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Curve_Digital" id="mwARA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Curve Digital">
      Curve Digital
     </a>
     Dominic Wheatley expressed his interest alongside the company in the series, saying "I'd be very happy to have a James Bond licence. We could do a cracking game around that," adding that these opportunities are overlooked by the bigger firms, since
     <a href="./Electronic_Arts" id="mwARE" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Electronic Arts">
      Electronic Arts
     </a>
     and
     <a href="./Activision" id="mwARI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Activision">
      Activision
     </a>
     have their own
     <a href="./Intellectual_property" id="mwARM" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Intellectual property">
      IPs
     </a>
     and no longer want to "promote someone else's brand."
     <sup about="#mwt199" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-37"}}' id="cite_ref-37" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-37" id="mwARQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 37;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwARU">
        [37]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwARY">
     In November 2020,
     <a href="./IO_Interactive" id="mwARc" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="IO Interactive">
      IO Interactive
     </a>
     announced
     <i id="mwARg">
      Project 007
     </i>
     , a brand new
     <a href="./James_Bond" id="mwARk" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond">
      James Bond
     </a>
     video game, working closely with licensors
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./MGM" id="mwARo" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="MGM">
      MGM
     </a>
     and
     <a href="./Eon_Productions" id="mwARs" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Eon Productions">
      Eon Productions
     </a>
     . IO described the game as a "wholly original Bond story" where "players will step into the shoes of the world's favorite Secret Agent to earn their 00 status in the very first Bond origin story."
     <sup about="#mwt205" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-38"}}' id="cite_ref-38" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-38" id="mwARw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 38;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAR0">
        [38]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <sup about="#mwt209" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-39"}}' id="cite_ref-39" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-39" id="mwAR4" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 39;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAR8">
        [39]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game is currently in pre-production with no set release window.
    </p>
   </section>
  </section>
  <section data-mw-section-id="7" id="mwASA">
   <h2 id="Cancelled_games">
    Cancelled games
   </h2>
   <dl id="mwASE">
    <dt id="mwASI">
     <i id="mwASM">
      Octopussy
     </i>
     (1983)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwASQ">
    Shortly after
    <i id="mwASU">
     <a href="./James_Bond_007_(1983_video_game)" id="mwASY" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007 (1983 video game)">
      James Bond 007
     </a>
    </i>
    was released in 1983 by Parker Brothers, another video game was announced, titled
    <i id="mwASc">
     Octopussy
    </i>
    , based on the film of the same name. The game was planned for release on the Atari 2600 System, Mattel Intellivision, and compatible systems. Set for release in the summer of 1983, it was cancelled for unknown reasons shortly after it was announced by Parker Brothers.
    <sup about="#mwt214" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-40"}}' id="cite_ref-40" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-40" id="mwASg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 40;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwASk">
       [40]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwASo">
    <dt id="mwASs">
     <i id="mwASw">
      GoldenEye 007
     </i>
     (1997; 2008)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAS0">
    A racing version of
    <i id="mwAS4">
     <a href="./GoldenEye_007_(1997_video_game)" id="mwAS8" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye 007 (1997 video game)">
      GoldenEye 007
     </a>
    </i>
    was announced for the
    <a href="./Virtual_Boy" id="mwATA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Virtual Boy">
     Virtual Boy
    </a>
    .
    <sup about="#mwt221" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-41"}}' id="cite_ref-41" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-41" id="mwATE" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 41;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwATI">
       [41]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    The game was cancelled in 1996.
    <sup about="#mwt225" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-42"}}' id="cite_ref-42" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-42" id="mwATM" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 42;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwATQ">
       [42]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    <sup about="#mwt229" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-43"}}' id="cite_ref-43" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-43" id="mwATU" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 43;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwATY">
       [43]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <p id="mwATc">
    A remastered version of the
    <a href="./Nintendo_64" id="mwATg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Nintendo 64">
     Nintendo 64
    </a>
    game
    <i id="mwATk">
     GoldenEye 007
    </i>
    by
    <a href="./Rare_(company)" id="mwATo" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Rare (company)">
     Rare
    </a>
    was scheduled for release on
    <a href="./Xbox_360" id="mwATs" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Xbox 360">
     Xbox 360
    </a>
    's
    <a href="./Xbox_Live_Arcade" id="mwATw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Xbox Live Arcade">
     Live Arcade
    </a>
    on 27 February 2008, but
    <a href="./Microsoft" id="mwAT0" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Microsoft">
     Microsoft
    </a>
    (who acquired Rare and their intellectual properties in 2002) couldn't get the publishing rights from the intellectual property owners,
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Danjaq,_LLC" id="mwAT4" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Danjaq, LLC">
     Danjaq, LLC
    </a>
    , resulting in the cancelation of the project, despite being nearly completed.
    <sup about="#mwt235" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-44"}}' id="cite_ref-44" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-44" id="mwAT8" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 44;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAUA">
       [44]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    It was rumored that
    <a href="./Nintendo" id="mwAUE" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Nintendo">
     Nintendo
    </a>
    (the publisher of the original title) or
    <a href="./Activision" id="mwAUI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Activision">
     Activision
    </a>
    (who had exclusive rights to publish video games based on the James Bond franchise at the time) may have been involved in the project's cancellation, but no sources confirm the rumor. Despite this, in January 2021, a near-final build of the game was leaked online from an unknown source, which lead to many players playing the ROM via emulation.
    <sup about="#mwt239" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-45"}}' id="cite_ref-45" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-45" id="mwAUM" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 45;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAUQ">
       [45]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAUU">
    <dt id="mwAUY">
     <i id="mwAUc">
      Tomorrow Never Dies: The Mission Continues
     </i>
     (1998)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAUg">
    The original VHS release of
    <i id="mwAUk">
     <a href="./Tomorrow_Never_Dies" id="mwAUo" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">
      Tomorrow Never Dies
     </a>
    </i>
    featured a brief trailer with
    <a href="./Desmond_Llewelyn" id="mwAUs" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Desmond Llewelyn">
     Desmond Llewelyn
    </a>
    which highlighted a game that would "start where the film ends".
    <sup about="#mwt247" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-46"}}' id="cite_ref-46" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-46" id="mwAUw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 46;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAU0">
       [46]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    Footage shows Bond skiing, scuba diving and driving in third person and on a
    <a href="./First-person_shooter" id="mwAU4" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="First-person shooter">
     first-person
    </a>
    shooting mission.
    <sup about="#mwt251" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-47"}}' id="cite_ref-47" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-47" id="mwAU8" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 47;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAVA">
       [47]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    The game was to come out on
    <a href="./PlayStation_(console)" id="mwAVE" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="PlayStation (console)">
     PlayStation
    </a>
    and PC in the fall of 1998 and was being made by
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./MGM_Interactive" id="mwAVI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="MGM Interactive">
     MGM Interactive
    </a>
    , not
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./EA" id="mwAVM" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="EA">
     EA
    </a>
    ; EA was not involved in Bond until November of that year.
    <sup about="#mwt255" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-48"}}' id="cite_ref-48" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-48" id="mwAVQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 48;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAVU">
       [48]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    Because MGM's motion picture division had licensed exclusive James Bond console rights to Nintendo (for
    <i id="mwAVY">
     GoldenEye 007
    </i>
    for the Nintendo 64), MGM had to buy some of their rights back from Nintendo in order to make the game.
    <sup about="#mwt259" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-49"}}' id="cite_ref-49" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-49" id="mwAVc" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 49;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAVg">
       [49]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <p id="mwAVk">
    A
    <i id="mwAVo">
     <a href="./Tomorrow_Never_Dies_(video_game)" id="mwAVs" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Tomorrow Never Dies (video game)">
      Tomorrow Never Dies
     </a>
    </i>
    game was released on 16 November 1999, distributed by EA, but with notable differences from the 1998 attempt. The game was a
    <a href="./Third-person_shooter" id="mwAVw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Third-person shooter">
     third-person shooter
    </a>
    with no scuba diving level. The story follows the plot of the film, not the continuation that had been planned.
   </p>
   <p id="mwAV0">
    A level in the game sees Bond skiing down a mountain and killing a Japanese terrorist named Sotoshi Isagura (who had featured very briefly in the film), while on another stage Bond has a driving mission in Switzerland. These were not from the film and may have survived from the 'continuation' story.
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAV4">
    <dt id="mwAV8">
     <i id="mwAWA">
      The World Is Not Enough
     </i>
     (2000)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAWE">
    A game based on the 1999 film
    <i id="mwAWI">
     The World Is Not Enough
    </i>
    film and using the
    <i id="mwAWM">
     <a href="./Quake_III_Arena" id="mwAWQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Quake III Arena">
      Quake III Arena
     </a>
    </i>
    engine for the
    <a href="./Personal_computer" id="mwAWU" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Personal computer">
     PC
    </a>
    and
    <a href="./PlayStation_2" id="mwAWY" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="PlayStation 2">
     PlayStation 2
    </a>
    was cancelled in favor for
    <i id="mwAWc">
     <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Agent_Under_Fire" id="mwAWg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Agent Under Fire">
      Agent Under Fire
     </a>
    </i>
    .
    <sup about="#mwt265" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-50"}}' id="cite_ref-50" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-50" id="mwAWk" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 50;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAWo">
       [50]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    Electronic Arts thought, by 2001, that too much time has passed since the release of the film, and that fans would be no longer interested in the product as talks of the succeeding film in the series,
    <i id="mwAWs">
     <a href="./Die_Another_Day" id="mwAWw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Die Another Day">
      Die Another Day
     </a>
    </i>
    , were taking place.
    <sup about="#mwt269" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-51"}}' id="cite_ref-51" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-51" id="mwAW0" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 51;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAW4">
       [51]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAW8">
    <dt id="mwAXA">
     <i id="mwAXE">
      007 Racing
     </i>
     sequel (2001)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAXI">
    A PlayStation 2 sequel to
    <i id="mwAXM">
     <a href="./007_Racing" id="mwAXQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007 Racing">
      007 Racing
     </a>
    </i>
    was rumoured to be in development.
    <sup about="#mwt274" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-52"}}' id="cite_ref-52" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-52" id="mwAXU" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 52;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAXY">
       [52]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAXc">
    <dt id="mwAXg">
     <i id="mwAXk">
      Bond6
     </i>
     (2005)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAXo">
    EA Games began conceptual work on the game in 2003, under the working title of
    <i id="mwAXs">
     Bond6
    </i>
    . The game was originally meant to be released in 2005, set to star
    <a href="./Pierce_Brosnan" id="mwAXw" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Pierce Brosnan">
     Pierce Brosnan
    </a>
    as
    <a class="mw-redirect" href="./James_Bond_(character)" id="mwAX0" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond (character)">
     James Bond
    </a>
    . A video game adaptation of
    <i id="mwAX4">
     <a href="./From_Russia_with_Love_(video_game)" id="mwAX8" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="From Russia with Love (video game)">
      From Russia with Love
     </a>
    </i>
    began development when Brosnan announced that he was stepping down from the role, which ended plans for
    <i id="mwAYA">
     Bond6
    </i>
    . The opening level planned for the former was retooled for the latter, and CGI work intended for the game was reused in television commercials for
    <i id="mwAYE">
     GoldenEye: Rogue Agent
    </i>
    .
    <sup about="#mwt279" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-53"}}' id="cite_ref-53" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-53" id="mwAYI" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 53;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAYM">
       [53]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAYQ">
    <dt id="mwAYU">
     <i id="mwAYY">
      Casino Royale
     </i>
     (2006)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAYc">
    A game was in development based on
    <a href="./Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" id="mwAYg" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">
     the film of the same name
    </a>
    .
    <a href="./Daniel_Craig" id="mwAYk" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Daniel Craig">
     Daniel Craig
    </a>
    , in character as Bond, was going to give his voice and likeness to the video game. It was set to release on the PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360 platforms. The game was 15% developed when the project was cancelled, as Electronic Arts would not finish it by the film's release in November 2006. Later, unfinished development screenshots from the Venice level were uncovered.
    <sup about="#mwt283" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Fritz"}}' id="cite_ref-Fritz_21-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-Fritz-21" id="mwAYo" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 21;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAYs">
       [21]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    <sup about="#mwt284" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"EA CR"}}' id="cite_ref-EA_CR_19-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-EA_CR-19" id="mwAYw" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAY0">
       [19]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    <sup about="#mwt285" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"LostGame"}}' id="cite_ref-LostGame_20-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-LostGame-20" id="mwAY4" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 20;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAY8">
       [20]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    Activision's debut in the series,
    <i id="mwAZA">
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Quantum_of_Solace_(video_game)" id="mwAZE" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Quantum of Solace (video game)">
      Quantum of Solace
     </a>
    </i>
    , combines the storylines of
    <i id="mwAZI">
     Casino Royale
    </i>
    and
    <i id="mwAZM">
     Quantum of Solace
    </i>
    .
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAZQ">
    <dt id="mwAZU">
     <i id="mwAZY">
      Blood Stone
     </i>
     sequel (2011)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAZc">
    In December 2010, some screenshots and a video were leaked online that depicted a new James Bond game, which shared similar gameplay to its predecessor,
    <i id="mwAZg">
     Blood Stone
    </i>
    . Reportedly, the project had been in development by
    <a href="./Raven_Software" id="mwAZk" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Raven Software">
     Raven Software
    </a>
    , but was postponed six months prior to the leak, at which point the game was believed to be back in development. However, the game was ultimately cancelled due to
    <i id="mwAZo">
     Blood Stone's
    </i>
    poor sales.
    <sup about="#mwt290" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-54"}}' id="cite_ref-54" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-54" id="mwAZs" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 54;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAZw">
       [54]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
   <dl id="mwAZ0">
    <dt id="mwAZ4">
     <i id="mwAZ8">
      Skyfall
     </i>
     (2012)
    </dt>
   </dl>
   <p id="mwAaA">
    In January 2012, it was announced that a video game based on
    <i id="mwAaE">
     <a href="./Skyfall" id="mwAaI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Skyfall">
      Skyfall
     </a>
    </i>
    would be released by Activision.
    <sup about="#mwt296" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-55"}}' id="cite_ref-55" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-55" id="mwAaM" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 55;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAaQ">
       [55]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
    Ultimately, a downloadable level based on
    <i id="mwAaU">
     Skyfall
    </i>
    was released for Activision's
    <i id="mwAaY">
     <a href="./007_Legends" id="mwAac" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007 Legends">
      007 Legends
     </a>
    </i>
    , although a full game was not released.
    <sup about="#mwt300" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-56"}}' id="cite_ref-56" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
     <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-56" id="mwAag" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 56;">
      <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAak">
       [56]
      </span>
     </a>
    </sup>
   </p>
  </section>
  <section data-mw-section-id="8" id="mwAao">
   <h2 id="Other_games">
    Other games
   </h2>
   <section data-mw-section-id="9" id="mwAas">
    <h3 id="Mobile_and_smartphone_games">
     Mobile and smartphone games
    </h3>
    <p id="mwAaw">
     Since 2002, games featuring the Bond character and the
     <i id="mwAa0">
      007
     </i>
     trademark have been published and distributed on mobile phones. The first two are based on action sequences from
     <i id="mwAa4">
      <a href="./Die_Another_Day" id="mwAa8" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Die Another Day">
       Die Another Day
      </a>
     </i>
     , one of them is titled
     <i id="mwAbA">
      Hover Chase
     </i>
     and the other is
     <i id="mwAbE">
      Ice Racer
     </i>
     . Both were published by
     <a href="./Vodafone" id="mwAbI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Vodafone">
      Vodafone
     </a>
     .
    </p>
    <p id="mwAbM">
     With the official reboot of the film franchise in 2006,
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Sony_Online_Entertainment" id="mwAbQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Sony Online Entertainment">
      Sony Online Entertainment
     </a>
     released a side-scroll action game based on
     <i id="mwAbU">
      <a href="./Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" id="mwAbY" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">
       Casino Royale
      </a>
     </i>
     developed by
     <a href="./Glu_Mobile" id="mwAbc" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Glu Mobile">
      Glu Mobile
     </a>
     , following a storyline inspired by the film. Similarly, an identical tie-in based on
     <i id="mwAbg">
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Quantum_of_Solace_(film)" id="mwAbk" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Quantum of Solace (film)">
       Quantum of Solace
      </a>
     </i>
     was released in 2008 by the same team. The same year, Sony Online Entertainment Los Angeles developed and published an arcade
     <a href="./Fighting_game" id="mwAbo" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Fighting game">
      fighting game
     </a>
     to coincide with the aforementioned film, entitled
     <i id="mwAbs">
      Top Agent
     </i>
     .
    </p>
    <p id="mwAbw">
     In 2014, it was reported that Glu Mobile was working on another mobile game bearing the James Bond license.
     <sup about="#mwt308" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-57"}}' id="cite_ref-57" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-57" id="mwAb0" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 57;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAb4">
        [57]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     A year later, its title was revealed as
     <i id="mwAb8">
      World of Espionage
     </i>
     ,
     <sup about="#mwt312" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-58"}}' id="cite_ref-58" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-58" id="mwAcA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 58;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAcE">
        [58]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     a
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Point-and-click_Adventure" id="mwAcI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Point-and-click Adventure">
      point-and-click
     </a>
     game retelling several previous storylines from the film series, debuting an
     <a href="./Early_access" id="mwAcM" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Early access">
      early access
     </a>
     mode in July 2015 and releasing a full version of the game in November later that year.
     <sup about="#mwt316" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-59"}}' id="cite_ref-59" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-59" id="mwAcQ" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 59;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAcU">
        [59]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The game, after being universally panned for its uninspired content, was removed from the online mobile stores in December 2016 and Glu Mobile pulled the plug on the title.
     <sup about="#mwt320" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-60"}}' id="cite_ref-60" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-60" id="mwAcY" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 60;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAcc">
        [60]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="10" id="mwAcg">
    <h3 id="Fanmade_remakes">
     Fanmade remakes
    </h3>
    <style about="#mwt321" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See","href":"./Template:See"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"GoldenEye: Source"}},"i":0}}]}' data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096" id="mwAck" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion">
     .mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}
    </style>
    <div about="#mwt321" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" id="mwAco" role="note">
     Further information:
     <a href="./GoldenEye:_Source" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye: Source">
      GoldenEye: Source
     </a>
    </div>
    <p id="mwAcs">
     With the popularity laid by
     <i id="mwAcw">
      <a href="./GoldenEye_007_(1997_video_game)" id="mwAc0" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye 007 (1997 video game)">
       GoldenEye 007
      </a>
     </i>
     in 1997 on the Nintendo 64, fans of the video game have made many attempts to remake or recreate the title with updated makeovers on current engines over time. But, only one project succeeded. Entitled
     <i id="mwAc4">
      <a href="./GoldenEye:_Source" id="mwAc8" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="GoldenEye: Source">
       GoldenEye: Source
      </a>
     </i>
     , the game entered development in 2005 and officially saw its international release in 2010, five years after being in
     <a href="./Software_release_life_cycle#Beta" id="mwAdA" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Software release life cycle">
      beta mode
     </a>
     hosted by the
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Source_(engine)" id="mwAdE" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Source (engine)">
      Source
     </a>
     engine. It is a
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Mod_(computer_gaming)#Total_conversion" id="mwAdI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Mod (computer gaming)">
      total conversion mod
     </a>
     based on the multiplayer mode from the aforementioned title.
    </p>
    <p id="mwAdM">
     A different team initiated similar attempts in 2013 to port the multiplayer mode from
     <i id="mwAdQ">
      <a href="./James_Bond_007:_Nightfire" id="mwAdU" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond 007: Nightfire">
       Nightfire
      </a>
     </i>
     (2002) to the Source engine, hoping to release it on
     <a href="./Steam_(service)" id="mwAdY" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Steam (service)">
      Steam
     </a>
     under the title
     <i id="mwAdc">
      Nightfire: Source
     </i>
     . The project, as of today, remains in development.
     <sup about="#mwt329" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-61"}}' id="cite_ref-61" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-61" id="mwAdg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 61;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAdk">
        [61]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <sup about="#mwt333" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-62"}}' id="cite_ref-62" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-62" id="mwAdo" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 62;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAds">
        [62]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwAdw">
     To commemorate the video game's 25th anniversary, another project based on
     <i id="mwAd0">
      GoldenEye 007
     </i>
     entered development in 2017 on
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./Unreal_Engine_4" id="mwAd4" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Unreal Engine 4">
      Unreal Engine 4
     </a>
     , with the aim of releasing it sometime in August 2022, based on the title's
     <a href="./Single-player_video_game" id="mwAd8" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Single-player video game">
      single-player
     </a>
     campaign.
     <sup about="#mwt340" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-63"}}' id="cite_ref-63" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-63" id="mwAeA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 63;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAeE">
        [63]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     However, in August 2020, the team received a
     <a href="./Cease_and_desist" id="mwAeI" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Cease and desist">
      cease and desist
     </a>
     letter from
     <a href="./Danjaq" id="mwAeM" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Danjaq">
      Danjaq
     </a>
     , forbidding the remake and stripping its use of any licensed asset related to the property, including
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./James_Bond_(film_character)" id="mwAeQ" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="James Bond (film character)">
      James Bond
     </a>
     and related characters.
     <sup about="#mwt344" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-64"}}' id="cite_ref-64" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-64" id="mwAeU" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 64;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAeY">
        [64]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     The project was reborn as
     <i id="mwAec">
      Spies Don't Die
     </i>
     – an original experience "inspired by 90s first-person shooters".
     <sup about="#mwt348" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-65"}}' id="cite_ref-65" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-65" id="mwAeg" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 65;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAek">
        [65]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
   </section>
   <section data-mw-section-id="11" id="mwAeo">
    <h3 id="Appearance_in_other_media">
     Appearance in other media
    </h3>
    <p id="mwAes">
     Downloadable content featuring a pack of cars used in the James Bond films is available in
     <i id="mwAew">
      <a href="./Forza_Horizon_4" id="mwAe0" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Forza Horizon 4">
       Forza Horizon 4
      </a>
     </i>
     , officially branded and licensed by Danjaq, LLC.
     <sup about="#mwt354" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-66"}}' id="cite_ref-66" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-66" id="mwAe4" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 66;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAe8">
        [66]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
     <sup about="#mwt358" class="mw-ref reference" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-67"}}' id="cite_ref-67" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref">
      <a href="./James_Bond_in_video_games#cite_note-67" id="mwAfA" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 67;">
       <span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAfE">
        [67]
       </span>
      </a>
     </sup>
    </p>
    <p id="mwAfI">
     <a href="./Sean_Connery" id="mwAfM" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Sean Connery">
      Sean Connery
     </a>
     's James Bond is parodied in
     <i id="mwAfQ">
      <a href="./Broforce" id="mwAfU" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Broforce">
       Broforce
      </a>
     </i>
     as a playable character, Double Bro Seven, whose name is a pun on Bond's code number
     <a class="mw-redirect" href="./007" id="mwAfY" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="007">
      007
     </a>
     . Just like the actual Bond, he wears a tuxedo and uses a pistol. Unlike other characters in the game, he has a variety of special skills, including a martini, needed for a trophy called "
     <a href="./Shaken,_not_stirred" id="mwAfc" rel="mw:WikiLink" title="Shaken, not stirred">
      Shaken, not stirred
     </a>
     ", which is a joke on a famous Bond catchphrase.
    </p>
   </section>
  </section>
  <section data-mw-section-id="12" id="mwAfg">
   <h2 id="References">
    References
